There\\n11: /// is no \\\"pass\\\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\\n13: /// a pass. As there is no\\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\\n18: /// single The only currently\\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n111:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\\n113:   }\\n114: };\\n115: \\n116: namespace detail {\\n117: \\n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\\n121:           typename... It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\\n153: /// pass pipeline.\\n154: ///\\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\\\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\\n164: public:\\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\\n167: \\n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\\n169:   // assignment. However, using = default triggers linker errors due to the\\n170:   // explicit instantiations below. Find away to use the default and remove the\\n171:   // duplicated code here.\\n172:   PassManager(PassManager &&Arg) : Passes(std::move(Arg.Passes)) {}\\n173: \\n174:   PassManager &operator=(PassManager &&RHS) {\\n175:     Passes = std::move(RHS.Passes);\\n176:     return *this;\\n177:   }\\n178: \\n179:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n180:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n181:     ListSeparator LS(\\\",\\\");\\n182:     for (auto &P : Passes) {\\n183:       OS << LS;\\n184:       P->printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\\n185:     }\\n186:   }\\n187: \\n188:   /// Run all of the passes in this manager over the given unit of IR.\\n189:   /// ExtraArgs are passed to each pass.\\n190:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\\n191:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\\n202:   }\\n203: \\n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. This is because we don't have\\n206:   /// use cases rely on executing nested pass managers. Doing this could\\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\\n209:   template Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\\n214:   }\\n215: \\n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\\n218: \\n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\\n220: \\n221: protected:\\n222:   using PassConceptT =\\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n224: \\n225: There\n11: /// is no \"pass\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\n18: /// single module provided.\n19: ///\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\n21: /// modules and functions.\n22: ///\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\n24: ///   a Function.\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\n26: ///\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \"Value Semantics and Concept-based\n29: /// Polymorphism\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \"Inheritance Is The Base\n30: /// Class of Evil\") by Sean Parent:\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\n32: /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\n33: /// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\n34: ///\n35: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n36: \n37: #ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n38: #define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n39: \n40: #include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n41: #include \"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\"\n42: #include \"llvm/ADT/StringExtras.h\"\n43: #include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n44: #include \"llvm/ADT/TinyPtrVector.h\"\n45: #include \"llvm/IR/Analysis.h\"\n46: #include \"llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h\"\n47: #include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n48: #include \"llvm/Support/TypeName.h\"\n49: #include <cassert>\n50: #include <cstring>\n51: #include <list>\n52: #include <memory>\n53: #include <tuple>\n54: #include <type_traits>\n55: #include <utility>\n56: #include <vector>\n57: \n58: namespace llvm {\n59: \n60: class Function;\n61: class Module;\n62: \n63: // Forward declare the analysis manager template.\n64: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\n65: \n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\n67: /// passes.\n68: ///\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\n70: template <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\n72:   static StringRef name() {\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\n74:                   \"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\");\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\n76:     Name.consume_front(\"llvm::\");\n77:     return Name;\n78:   }\n79: \n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\n81:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\n84:     OS << PassName;\n85:   }\n86: };\n87: \n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\n89: ///\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\c PassInfoMixin.\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\n95:   ///\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\n99:   ///\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\c AnalysisKey\n101:   /// member called \\c Key.\n102:   ///\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. If we ever remove that build\n108:   /// configuration, this mixin can provide the static key as well.\n109:   static AnalysisKey *ID() {\n110:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<AnalysisInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\n111:                   \"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\");\n112:     return &DerivedT::Key;\n113:   }\n114: };\n115: \n116: namespace detail {\n117: \n118: /// Actual unpacker of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult,\n119: /// passes only those tuple arguments that are mentioned in index_sequence.\n120: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\n121:           typename... ArgTs, size_t... Ns>\n122: typename PassT::Result\n123: getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple(AnalysisManagerT &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\n124:                              std::tuple<ArgTs...> Args,\n125:                              std::index_sequence<Ns...>) {\n126:   (void)Args;\n127:   return AM.template getResult<PassT>(IR, std::get<Ns>(Args)...);\n128: }\n129: \n130: /// Helper for *partial* unpacking of extra arguments in getAnalysisResult.\n131: ///\n132: /// Arguments passed in tuple come from PassManager, so they might have extra\n133: /// arguments after those AnalysisManager's ExtraArgTs ones that we need to\n134: /// pass to getResult.\n135: template <typename PassT, typename IRUnitT, typename... AnalysisArgTs,\n136:           typename... MainArgTs>\n137: typename PassT::Result\n138: getAnalysisResult(AnalysisManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisArgTs...> &AM, IRUnitT &IR,\n139:                   std::tuple<MainArgTs...> Args) {\n140:   return (getAnalysisResultUnpackTuple<\n141:           PassT, IRUnitT>)(AM, IR, Args,\n142:                            std::index_sequence_for<AnalysisArgTs...>{});\n143: }\n144: \n145: } // namespace detail\n146: \n147: /// Manages a sequence of passes over a particular unit of IR.\n148: ///\n149: /// A pass manager contains a sequence of passes to run over a particular unit\n150: /// of IR (e.g. Functions, Modules). It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\n153: /// pass pipeline.\n154: ///\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\n164: public:\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\n167: \n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\n169:   // assignment. However, using = default triggers linker errors due to the\n170:   // explicit instantiations below. Find away to use the default and remove the\n171:   // duplicated code here.\n172:   PassManager(PassManager &&Arg) : Passes(std::move(Arg.Passes)) {}\n173: \n174:   PassManager &operator=(PassManager &&RHS) {\n175:     Passes = std::move(RHS.Passes);\n176:     return *this;\n177:   }\n178: \n179:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\n180:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\n181:     ListSeparator LS(\",\");\n182:     for (auto &P : Passes) {\n183:       OS << LS;\n184:       P->printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\n185:     }\n186:   }\n187: \n188:   /// Run all of the passes in this manager over the given unit of IR.\n189:   /// ExtraArgs are passed to each pass.\n190:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\n191:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs);\n192: \n193:   template <typename PassT>\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\n196:     using PassModelT =\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\n202:   }\n203: \n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. This is because we don't have\n206:   /// use cases rely on executing nested pass managers. Doing this could\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\n209:   template <typename PassT>\n210:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\n211:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\n212:     for (auto &P : Pass.Passes)\n213:       Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\n214:   }\n215: \n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\n218: \n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\n220: \n221: protected:\n222:   using PassConceptT =\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\n224: \n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\n226: };\n227: \n228: template <typename IRUnitT>\n229: void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace(raw_ostream &OS, const IRUnitT &IR);\n230: \n231: template <>\n232: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Module>(raw_ostream &OS,\n233:                                                    const Module &IR);\n234: \n235: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Module>;\n236: \n237: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over modules.\n238: using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;\n239: \n240: template <>\n241: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Function>(raw_ostream &OS,\n242:                                                      const Function &IR);\n243: \n244: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Function>;\n245: \n246: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over functions.\n247: using FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function>;\n248: \n249: /// A container for analyses that lazily runs them and caches their\n250: /// results.\n251: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h%3FL1-250"}}}

It requires the pass to\n69: /// be a copyable object.\n70: template <typename IRUnitT, typename PassT, typename AnalysisManagerT,\n71:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\n72: struct PassModel : PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...> {\n73:   explicit PassModel(PassT Pass) : Pass(std::move(Pass)) {}\n74:   // We have to explicitly define all the special member functions because MSVC\n75:   // refuses to generate them.\n76:   PassModel(const PassModel &Arg) : Pass(Arg.Pass) {}\n77:   PassModel(PassModel &&Arg) : Pass(std::move(Arg.Pass)) {}\n78: \n79:   friend void swap(PassModel &LHS, PassModel &RHS) {\n80:     using std::swap;\n81:     swap(LHS.Pass, RHS.Pass);\n82:   }\n83: \n84:   PassModel &operator=(PassModel RHS) {\n85:     swap(*this, RHS);\n86:     return *this;\n87:   }\n88: \n89:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\n90:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs) override {\n91:     return Pass.run(IR, AM, ExtraArgs...);\n92:   }\n93: \n94:   void printPipeline(\n95:       raw_ostream &OS,\n96:       function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) override {\n97:     Pass.printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\n98:   }\n99: \n100:   StringRef name() const override { return PassT::name(); }\n101: \n102:   template <typename T>\n103:   using has_required_t = decltype(std::declval<T &>().isRequired());\n104: \n105:   template <typename T> static bool passIsRequiredImpl() {\n106:     if constexpr (is_detected<has_required_t, T>::value)\n107:       return T::isRequired();\n108:     return false;\n109:   }\n110: \n111:   bool isRequired() const override { return passIsRequiredImpl<PassT>(); }\n112: \n113:   PassT Pass;\n114: };\n115: \n116: /// Abstract concept of an analysis result.\n117: ///\n118: /// This concept is parameterized over the IR unit that this result pertains\n119: /// to.\n120: template <typename IRUnitT, typename InvalidatorT>\n121: struct AnalysisResultConcept {\n122:   virtual ~AnalysisResultConcept() = default;\n123: \n124:   /// Method to try and mark a result as invalid.\n125:   ///\n126:   /// When the outer analysis manager detects a change in some underlying\n127:   /// unit of the IR, it will call this method on all of the results cached.\n128:   ///\n129:   /// \\p PA is a set of preserved analyses which can be used to avoid\n130:   /// invalidation because the pass which changed the underlying IR took care\n131:   /// to update or preserve the analysis result in some way.\n132:   ///\n133:   /// \\p Inv is typically a \\c AnalysisManager::Invalidator object that can be\n134:   /// used by a particular analysis result to discover if other analyses\n135:   /// results are also invalidated in the event that this result depends on\n136:   /// them. Manager Registration and Execution Chain\\n\\nThe LLVM pass management system uses a sophisticated template-based architecture to support modular and composable optimization passes. Here's the complete registration and execution chain:\\n\\n### 1. PassManager Template (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h, line 162)\\nThe core `PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>` template provides the infrastructure for managing sequences of passes. Key methods:\\n- `addPass(PassT &&Pass)` (line 195): Adds passes to the pipeline using a PassModel wrapper\\n- `run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM, ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs)` (line 190): Executes all passes in sequence over the given IR unit\\n- Common instantiations: `ModulePassManager` (line 238) for module-level passes and `FunctionPassManager` (line 247) for function-level passes\\n\\n### 2. PassConcept and PassModel (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h)\\nThe polymorphic dispatch system that enables type-erased pass storage:\\n- `PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>` (line 40): Abstract base class defining the polymorphic interface for passes\\n- `PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>` (line 72): Template wrapper that implements PassConcept for any pass type\\nWhen a pass is added via `addPass()`, it's wrapped in a PassModel and stored as a unique_ptr<PassConcept> in the Passes vector (line 225 of PassManager.h).\\n\\n### 3.
